- AIBrainstormingTheater: clamp(300px, 50vw, 500px)
- AnalyticsTheater: clamp(320px, 52vw, 520px)

AIEnhancement uses 56vw middle value while others use 50-52vw. This means AIEnhancement scales more aggressively with viewport width.

 Analyzing the responsive plugin configurations:

AIEnhancementStage:
- baselineWidth: 1120
- minScale: 0.32, maxScale: 1.2
- Uses GRID layout with explicit columns
- baseValues include leftColumn: 320, centerColumn: 220, rightColumn: 456

SchedulingStage:
- baselineWidth: 900 (MAX_CONTENT_WIDTH)
- minScale: 0.35, maxScale: 1.4
- Single centered content approach

AIBrainstormingStage:
- baselineWidth: 500 (MAX_CONTENT_WIDTH)
- minScale: 0.6, maxScale: 2.0
- Mobile overrides for minimum sizes

AnalyticsStage:
- baselineWidth: 960
- minScale: 0.25, maxScale: 1.2
- Grid layout but simpler (3 cards + chart)

CRITICAL ISSUE: AIEnhancement has baselineWidth of 1120 but minScale of 0.32, meaning it expects to scale down to ~358px effective width. But the GRID layout has FIXED column calculations that don't account for this extreme scaling.

 Looking at the grid template calculation in AIEnhancementStage:

layoutColumns computed property does this:
```typescript
return `${Math.round(cols.leftColumn)}px ${Math.round(cols.centerColumn)}px ${Math.round(cols.rightColumn)}px`
```

This creates PIXEL-based grid columns from scaled values. At minScale 0.32:
- leftColumn: 320 * 0.32 = 102px
- centerColumn: 220 * 0.32 = 70px
- rightColumn: 456 * 0.32 = 146px
- gap: 80 * 0.32 = 26px
- TOTAL: 102 + 70 + 146 + (2 * 26) = 370px

But also notice the grid plugin config:
```typescript
columns: 'minmax(0, 1fr) minmax(0, 2fr) minmax(0, 1fr)'
```

This creates a RATIO-based grid (1:2:1), but then layoutColumns OVERRIDES this with explicit pixel values!

The minmax(0, Xfr) is never actually used because the :style binding replaces gridTemplateColumns.

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 6/12 

 Looking at getTargetX calculation for flying cards:

```typescript
const getTargetX = (index: number) => {
  const layout = scaled.value
  const duplicateWidth = 100 * enhancementScale.value // 100 * 0.32 = 32px at minScale
  const maxInside = Math.max(1120 - duplicateWidth, layout.leftColumn + layout.centerColumn)
  const flight = layout.leftColumn + layout.gap + layout.centerColumn + layout.gap + Math.max(layout.rightColumn - duplicateWidth, layout.rightColumn * 0.5)
  const safeDistance = Math.min(flight, maxInside)
  return `${Math.round(safeDistance)}px`
}
```

At minScale (0.32):
- duplicateWidth = 32px
- maxInside = max(1120 - 32, 102 + 70) = max(1088, 172) = 1088px
- flight = 102 + 26 + 70 + 26 + max(146 - 32, 73) = 224 + max(114, 73) = 338px
- safeDistance = min(338, 1088) = 338px

But wait - the CONTAINER width is only ~370px total! The target is 338px which means the cards fly almost to the right edge, leaving only 32px. This doesn't account for the actual scaled container width.

  Thought 7/12 

 Comparing with SchedulingStage's approach:

SchedulingStage doesn't use a grid layout. It's a simple centered flex container with absolutely positioned children (clock at center, orbiting posts, indicator). All sizing is handled via the responsive plugin's scaled values passed as props.

Key difference: SchedulingStage has a single "content width" concept (900px baseline) and everything is positioned relative to CENTER with radius-based calculations. No complex grid columns to break down.

AIBrainstormingStage is similar - single centered content, absolutely positioned children relative to center, simpler scaling model.

AnalyticsStage uses grid BUT it's simpler - just "repeat(3, minmax(0, 1fr))" for cards, and the grid adapts naturally. The contentWidth is used as max-width, not as explicit column definitions.

  Thought 8/12 

 The proportionality problem:

AIEnhancementStage defines columns as:
- leftColumn: 320 (29% of 1120)
- centerColumn: 220 (20% of 1120)
- rightColumn: 456 (41% of 1120)
- gap: 80 each (7% each, 14% total for 2 gaps)
- Total: 1076 + 44 extra? Actually 320+220+456 = 996, plus 2*80 gaps = 1156

Wait, that's ALREADY over 1120 baseline! 996 + 160 = 1156px needed, but baseline is 1120px. The grid plugin config says 'minmax(0, 1fr) minmax(0, 2fr) minmax(0, 1fr)' which would be flexible, but the computed layoutColumns OVERRIDES this with fixed pixel values that don't fit.

At baseline (scale=1.0):
- Container width: 1120px
- Columns needed: 320 + 220 + 456 = 996px
- Gaps needed: 80 * 2 = 160px
- Total: 1156px
- Overflow: 36px!

The layout is ALREADY broken at baseline scale!

  Thought 9/12 

 Tracking issue at small scales:

The relationships plugin tracks "orb-to-cards" connections using:
- trackingMode: 'center-to-center'
- updateMode: 'raf'
- targets: { selector: '.card-item' }

TheaterBeams receives connections array and svgSize computed from theaterRef.getBoundingClientRect().

At minScale, the SVG size would be ~370px width, but the getTargetX calculations reference UNSCALED baseline dimensions (1120 in maxInside calculation). This creates a mismatch between:
1. Where the browser thinks elements are (scaled grid at ~370px)
2. Where the animation calculations think they should be (referencing 1120px baseline)

The connections array tracks actual DOM positions, so beams would draw correctly, but the flying card targets are calculated wrong.

 Core architectural difference causing issues:

Other theaters:
- Use CONTENT-WIDTH as constraint
- Elements positioned within that content area
- Scaling affects everything uniformly
- No explicit grid column definitions in pixels

AIEnhancementStage:
- Defines GRID COLUMNS as explicit pixel values
- Grid columns sum to MORE than baseline width
- Flying animation targets reference baseline dimensions
- Creates compound scaling errors (grid scaled, but targets reference unscaled values)

The aspect-ratio: 16/9 constraint at the stage level ALSO fights with the explicit pixel grid columns. If container is 400px wide due to aspect ratio, but grid columns want 1156px (at scale 1.0) or 370px (at scale 0.32), there's a conflict.

Likely behavior: The grid columns get squeezed into whatever width the aspect-ratio + min-height constraints create, causing proportions to break down.

  Thought 11/12 

 Why proportionality breaks at smaller sizes:

1. Grid columns defined as fixed pixels (320+220+456+160gaps = 1156px)
2. Container constrained by min-height: clamp(20rem, 50vw, 32rem) AND aspect-ratio: 16/9
3. At small viewport, clamp might give 320px height
4. With 16/9 aspect ratio: width = 320 * (16/9) = 569px
5. Grid wants 1156px at baseline, so scale = 569/1120 = 0.508
6. Scaled columns: 162+112+232+81gaps = 587px
7. But explicit pixel grid columns don't adapt to container - they overflow or squeeze

The "tracking" issue: Flying cards use getTargetX which references 1120 baseline in maxInside calculation, creating position mismatch with actual scaled grid.

The grid plugin's 'minmax(0, 1fr) minmax(0, 2fr) minmax(0, 1fr)' would be flexible, but layoutColumns OVERRIDES it with explicit pixels!

  Thought 12/12 

 Summary of core issues in AIEnhancementTheater vs other theaters:

**Fundamental Problem**: AIEnhancementStage uses HYBRID scaling approach that fights itself:
1. Responsive plugin calculates scale factor based on container width
2. Grid columns defined as EXPLICIT PIXELS from scaled values
3. Grid plugin defines flexible 'minmax(0, Xfr)' but layoutColumns overrides with pixels
4. Flying animation targets reference BASELINE dimensions (1120px) not actual scaled width
5. Grid column totals (996px + 160px gaps = 1156px) exceed baseline (1120px) = already broken
6. aspect-ratio: 16/9 + min-height constraints can create different widths than grid expects

**Why other theaters work**:
- Scheduling/Brainstorming: Centered content + absolute positioning, no grid conflicts
- Analytics: Grid with FLEXIBLE columns (repeat(3, minmax(0, 1fr))), not explicit pixels
- All use content-width as MAX constraint, not explicit column definitions

**Specific proportionality break**:
At small scales (0.32), grid columns become tiny (102+70+146+52gaps = 370px) but flying cards target 338px using calculations that reference 1120px baseline, creating position mismatches between where grid actually is vs where animations think it is.

This is an architectural mismatch, not just a scaling bug.

  Thought 1/15 

 Analyzing fix approaches for AIEnhancementTheater:

**Option 1: Match AnalyticsTheater Pattern**
- Replace explicit pixel columns with flexible grid: `repeat(3, minmax(0, 1fr))`
- Use max-width on container instead of explicit column widths
- Let browser handle proportions naturally
- Pro: Simple, proven pattern
- Con: Loses explicit control over column ratios (currently ~29%/20%/41%)

**Option 2: Match Scheduling/Brainstorming Pattern**
- Remove grid layout entirely
- Use centered container with absolute positioning
- Position zones using percentage offsets or transforms
- Pro: No grid conflicts, simpler coordinate space
- Con: Major rewrite, loses grid plugin benefits

**Option 3: Fix Grid Math + Coordinate Space**
- Adjust baseValues so columns + gaps = baseline (e.g., reduce gap from 80 to 62)
- Keep explicit pixel columns BUT make getTargetX use actual container width
- Track actual theater width and use it in animation calculations
- Pro: Preserves current structure
- Con: Still fighting aspect-ratio constraints, fragile

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 2/15 

 Evaluating Option 1 (Flexible Grid) deeper:

If we use `repeat(3, minmax(0, 1fr))`, we lose explicit column ratios. Currently:
- Left: 320px (29%)
- Center: 220px (20%)
- Right: 456px (41%)

With 1fr 1fr 1fr, we'd get 33%/33%/33% - center too wide, right too narrow.

Could use weighted fr units: `1fr 0.7fr 1.4fr` to approximate 29%/20%/41%
- 1 + 0.7 + 1.4 = 3.1 total
- Left: 1/3.1 = 32% (close to 29%)
- Center: 0.7/3.1 = 23% (close to 20%)
- Right: 1.4/3.1 = 45% (close to 41%)

But this still doesn't solve the animation coordinate space issue. getTargetX would still need to calculate based on actual container width, not baseline.

  Thought 3/15 

 Looking at how SchedulingTheater achieves its simplicity:

SchedulingStage doesn't use zones or grid. It's just:
- Theater container (flex, centered)
- Clock component (centered, absolute positioned)
- OrbitingPosts component (absolute positioned with transforms)
- PeakTimeIndicator (absolute positioned)

Everything uses a single reference point (center) and positions with transforms/radius calculations. The responsive plugin just scales the base values, no grid conflicts.

For AIEnhancement, we'd need:
- Single content container (flex, centered)
- Left zone: absolute positioned, left: 0 or negative translateX
- Center zone: absolute positioned, center (translateX(-50%))
- Right zone: absolute positioned, right: 0 or positive translateX

The three zones would be positioned based on percentage of content width or using specific offsets. Flying animations would use actual measured positions from DOM, not calculated coordinates.

  Thought 4/15 

 Analyzing what AIEnhancement actually needs:

Current visual layout:
- Left: Single post card shooting duplicates toward center
- Center: AI orb receiving posts, pulsing
- Right: 4 enhanced cards in 2x2 grid with beams from orb

Requirements:
- Orb must be centered
- Cards must have specific layout (2x2 grid)
- Flying animation must track from left to center to right
- Beams must draw from orb to each card dynamically
- Must scale proportionally at all sizes

Key insight: The RIGHT zone has internal complexity (2x2 grid), but the overall theater doesn't need grid layout. Only the FourCards component needs grid for its 2x2 arrangement.

Could use:
- Container: Single content area, max-width constraint
- Three zones: Absolute positioned within container
- Zone widths: Computed from responsive scaled values but positioned with transform/left/right
- FourCards internally uses its own grid for 2x2 layout

  Thought 5/15 

 Considering the relationships plugin dependency:

The relationships plugin is tracking:
```typescript
connections: [
  {
    id: 'orb-to-cards',
    source: { zone: 'center' },
    targets: { selector: '.card-item' },
    trackingMode: 'center-to-center',
    updateMode: 'raf'
  }
]
```

This relies on the grid plugin's zone definitions. If we remove grid, we'd need to:
- Either remove relationships plugin usage (lose automatic beam tracking)
- Or manually track element positions for beams
- Or modify how zones are defined (without grid plugin)

Actually, looking at the relationships plugin config - it doesn't care HOW zones are defined, just that they exist as data-zone attributes. The grid plugin provides zoneToStyle helper, but zones could be manually positioned.

So we could keep zone concept without grid layout system.

 Hybrid approach - keep some grid benefits but fix conflicts:

What if we:
1. Keep the grid plugin for zone definitions and relationships tracking
2. BUT use flexible fr units instead of explicit pixels
3. Fix the baseValues math so columns + gaps = baseline exactly
4. Fix getTargetX to use actual container dimensions instead of baseline

For grid columns, to maintain ~29%/20%/41% ratios:
- Target: 29% / 20% / 41% (plus gaps)
- With gaps: if gaps are 10% total (5% each), columns must be 90%
- Adjusted: 26% / 18% / 46% = 90%
- As fr units: 1.44fr 1fr 2.56fr (ratio of 26:18:46)

Or simpler: Use the existing minmax(0, 1fr) minmax(0, 2fr) minmax(0, 1fr) from grid plugin config and DON'T override with layoutColumns computed!

Then the browser naturally handles proportions, gap uses clamp(), and everything scales together.

  Thought 7/15 

 Examining what happens if we use the grid plugin's columns directly:

Grid plugin config defines:
```typescript
columns: 'minmax(0, 1fr) minmax(0, 2fr) minmax(0, 1fr)'
```

This creates a 1:2:1 ratio (25%/50%/25% without gaps).

But we're overriding this with:
```typescript
gridTemplateColumns: layoutColumns // "320px 220px 456px"
```

If we REMOVE the layoutColumns override and trust the grid plugin:
- Browser handles the 1:2:1 ratio naturally
- Gap uses the clamp() value from grid config
- Everything scales proportionally
- No pixel calculations needed

The ratio (1:2:1) is different from current (29%/20%/41%), but would it work visually?
- Left zone would get 25% (more space for shooting posts - actually better!)
- Center would get 50% (much more space around orb - might look too spacious)
- Right would get 25% (less space for 4 cards - might be cramped)

This might not preserve the intended visual balance.

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 8/15 

 Better approach - custom fr units to match current ratios:

Current effective ratios (accounting for content area):
- Left: 320px / 996px = 32%
- Center: 220px / 996px = 22%
- Right: 456px / 996px = 46%

To recreate this with fr units:
- 1.45fr (32%) : 1fr (22%) : 2.1fr (46%)
- Or normalize: 1.45fr 1fr 2.1fr

Grid plugin config would become:
```typescript
columns: '1.45fr 1fr 2.1fr'
```

Remove the layoutColumns override entirely - let grid plugin's columns value be used directly.

Then fix getTargetX to use actual container width:
```typescript
const containerWidth = theaterRef.value?.offsetWidth || 1120
const duplicateWidth = 100 * enhancementScale.value
// Calculate based on actual container and proportions
const leftColumnWidth = containerWidth * 0.32
const centerColumnWidth = containerWidth * 0.22
const gap = scaled.value.gap
const targetX = leftColumnWidth + gap + centerColumnWidth + gap + ...
```

This maintains visual proportions while using flexible layout.

  Thought 9/12 

 Wait, there's another issue - the gap value is being scaled too:

At baseline: gap = 80px
At scale 0.32: gap = 25.6px

But if we use fr units for columns, the gap needs to be in a compatible unit. CSS Grid gap property can use px, rem, %, etc.

If we use `gap: clamp(0.5rem, 2cqw, 2rem)` (from grid plugin config), this is responsive but independent of the responsive plugin's scale factor.

Actually, the grid plugin config already has:
```typescript
gap: 'clamp(0.5rem, 2cqw, 2rem)'
```

This is container query based (2cqw = 2% of container width), so it scales naturally with container size!

So the solution is:
1. Use weighted fr units: `1.45fr 1fr 2.1fr` in grid plugin config
2. Use the existing clamp() gap value
3. Remove layoutColumns override - don't bind gridTemplateColumns
4. Remove layoutGap override - don't bind gap
5. Fix getTargetX to use actual measured container dimensions

 Checking if we still need responsive plugin baseValues for columns/gaps:

Current responsive plugin config has:
```typescript
baseValues: {
  leftColumn: 320,
  centerColumn: 220,
  rightColumn: 456,
  gap: 80,
  ...
}
```

If we switch to fr units in grid, these baseValues are no longer used for layout. But they might be used by:
1. getTargetX calculations (currently yes)
2. Child component sizing (checking...)

ShootingPosts gets: `:max-width="scaled.leftColumn"` 
FourCards gets: `:max-width="scaled.rightColumn"`

So these scaled values ARE used as constraints on child components. We need to keep them in responsive plugin, but use them as max-width constraints, not grid column definitions.

The approach:
1. Grid columns use fr units for layout (proportional sizing)
2. Responsive scaled values provide max-width constraints to children
3. This decouples layout proportions from content constraints

 Finalizing the fix strategy:

**Minimal Change Approach (Recommended):**
1. Update grid plugin config: columns: '1.45fr 1fr 2.1fr' (matches current 32%/22%/46% ratios)
2. Remove layoutColumns computed override - let grid plugin's columns be used
3. Remove layoutGap computed override - let grid plugin's clamp() gap be used
4. Keep responsive plugin baseValues for child component max-width constraints
5. Fix getTargetX to measure actual container width instead of referencing baseline 1120px
6. Fix getTargetY to also use actual measurements if needed

**Why this works:**
- fr units = flexible, proportional layout that adapts to container
- clamp() gap = naturally responsive via container queries
- No explicit pixels = no overflow math errors
- Actual measurements = correct animation coordinates
- Maintains visual proportions and all plugin benefits

**Testing needed:**
- Verify at viewport widths: 320px, 768px, 1024px, 1920px
- Check animation targets land correctly
- Verify beams draw to correct positions
- Confirm no layout shift or overflow at any scale

   - Replace baseline references with actual proportions
   - Calculate based on actual rendered widths
